<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">In this paper, a detailed study is proposed on the properties of UHF RF identification (RFID) signals when the communication between the reader and tag is established. The main objective is to analyze the harmonics produced by the chip and radiated by the tag antenna. From experimentation, the characteristics of the nonlinearities contained in the signals are highlighted and linked to the theory of the backscattering in the RFID context. Several experiences taking into account the standards are proposed. Moreover, several commercial tags are considered in order to compare the observations. The used configuration, the experimental setup, and the protocols are described in detail. In particular, the generation of periodic and reproducible sequences of bits is introduced and its advantages are emphasized. Finally, contrarily to the classic approaches that tend to eliminate the harmonics generated by the rectifiers of tags, the great interest of the possible exploitation of backscattered harmonics is discussed in perspectives and some ideas of applications are given.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Rf identification (RFID) is a wireless data-collection technology that is becoming very popular in many applications and services, such as logistics, manufacturing, and security <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. The RFID system is composed by at least one reader and one tag; both interchanging information in a wireless mode. The reader acts as a base station, interacting with the tag in order to read or write information. In the case of passive UHF RFID tags, the reader transfers energy wirelessly to the tag by sending RF power that the tag must collect and transform into dc power to operate and respond using the backscattering modulation technique <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. The passive UHF RFID tag is composed by one antenna loaded by an integrated circuit (IC). One of the tasks that the IC performs is the rectification function, in which the IC obtains energy to operate as transponder. The rectifier converts the ac that comes in the RF waves sent by the reader into a dc, thus allowing the IC to do its other duties as transponder. The architecture of the rectifier is based on a Cockcroft–Walton circuit with two or more diode-based voltage doubler stages. These diodes determine the nonlinear behavior of the IC <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>. The goal of this paper is to evaluate the backscattered harmonics caused by these nonlinear diode effects. The study was done when the bidirectional communication reader–tag is fully established. Additionally, some analysis regarding the reader harmonics on the forward link were performed. An important contribution to the power spectral density (PSD) analysis was used to evaluate the backscattered harmonics. The PSD analysis configures the RFID air interface to produce a periodic sequence of bits on the tag response <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>. The quantified harmonic level is evaluated and its relation with the performance at fundamental frequency is analyzed. A dependency study on reader power, bits sequence structure, and channel in frequency hopping is performed. The experimental study is based on calculating the PSD of RFID signals at the harmonic frequencies in forward and return link in compliance of the EPC Class1 Gen2 UHF RFID standard <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>. The objective is to observe the characteristics of the modulated backscatter signal and assess the information carried by harmonics due to the nonlinearities. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a> explains the harmonic generation in passive UHF RFID tags. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a> proposes settings on the measurement procedure with special attention on the RFID air interface treatment. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a> describes the scatter capabilities of the measured tags. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5" class="fulltext-link">Section V</a> presents the properties of the PSD on the analysis of backscattered harmonics. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec6" class="fulltext-link">Section VI</a> shows the dependency analysis of the backscattered harmonics. Finally, in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec7" class="fulltext-link">Section VII</a>, some conclusions are drawn.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Harmonic Backscattering</h2></div><p>The reason why the harmonics currents are reradiated by the tag antenna can be explained looking to similar technologies at low-power rectification. The rectennas, devices conformed by one antenna loaded by one rectifier circuit commonly used for energy harvesting <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_2">[7]</a>, have a similar rectifier architecture as passive RFID tags. The difference is that the harvesting rectennas achieve efficiencies of RF to dc conversion up to 77% <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_2">[8]</a> thanks to the treatment of the nonlinearity effects with appropriate techniques of simulation as the harmonic balance (HB) for example. The HB considers the effect of the harmonics currents on the rectifier design also encouraging the effective matching with the antenna over a frequency range considering more than one impedance point minimizing the harmonic effect <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_2">[9]</a>. In passive UHF RFID tags contrary, the antenna design begins directly from the knowledge of one impedance value, which is the impedance of the IC at the fundamental frequency described on manufacturer data sheets <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_2">[10]</a>. The design process then tries to ensure the matching at the frequency of work, but there is no treatment of the harmonic currents received from the reader, which impairs the purity of the rectified dc signal, nor to those reflected in the antenna input as a result of the nonlinearity of the diodes in the return link <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_2">[11]</a>. This absence of nonlinear treatment, besides decreasing the rectifier efficiency of the tag <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_2">[12]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_2">[13]</a>, allows the tag antenna to radiate the reflected harmonic currents generated by the rectifier that triggers in backscattered harmonics.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Measurement Procedure</h2></div><p>The measurement procedure of backscattered harmonics is based on the observation of RFID signals in time domain, and the calculation of its PSD by applying the fast Fourier transform (FFT). <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a> shows the conceptual procedure. The FFT calculation is made over the carrier wave (CW) portion after the Query command shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>. The measurement procedure exploits directly the possibilities that the RFID air interface offers on its physical layer to facilitate the spectral analysis, the challenge is done by parameterizing the tag response in terms of a cyclic and reproducible signal, thus optimizing the PSD analysis.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1 </b><fig><p>Measurement procedure focused on the PSD analysis of UHF RFID signals.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2 </b><fig><p>Frames timing in forward and return link <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_3">[6]</a>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. RFID Air Interface</h3><p>The RFID air-interface standard provides parameter definitions for communications protocols within a common framework for globally accepted frequencies in RFID <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_3a">[14]</a>. The RFID air interface describes the way in which a tag communicates with a reader by wireless signals. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a> shows the multi-layer air interface model defined in the ISO standard 18000-1 <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_3a">[15]</a> using the open system interconnection (OSI) terms. The model is made of three layers: the application, communication, and physical layer <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_3a">[16]</a>.
</p><ul style="list-style-type:disc"><li><p>The application layer handles the information defined by the user. This could be an identifier allowing the reader to extract the corresponding information from the tagged object to read or write data into a data base (e.g., the title of a book).</p></li><li><p>The communication layer defines the way in which the readers and tags can communicate. Collision avoidance protocols are found in this layer, as well as an identifier that makes it possible to single out a specific tag for communication with a reader.</p></li><li><p>The physical layer defines the physical air interface, that is to say, frequency, operating channels, modulation, data encoding, timings, bit rate, preamble, and polarization.</p></li></ul>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3 </b><fig><p>Air interface protocol <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref16" id="context_ref_16_3a">[16]</a>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>One of the contributions of this work is to highlight the characteristics of the backscattering modulation to clearly interpret the time domain signals and its PSD calculation. Characteristics as backscattering link frequency (BLF), data encoding, and preamble are pre-configured on the treatment of the physical layer in the UHF RFID system.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3b"><h3>B. Configuration of the Physical Layer in the UHF RFID</h3><p>The configuration of the UHF RFID physical layer is based on the manipulation of the Query command frame sent by the reader. The pre-set Query command makes the tag responses with an easy understandable PSD, thus allowing to clearly identify its spectral content. It is intended that the BLF would be sufficiently higher to be distant from the carrier, and further, make the tag responds with a periodic sequence of bits whose duration is sufficient to perform the FFT.</p><p>The tag response to the Query command contains 16-bit pseudorandom called RN16. The RN16 response has a preamble with a well-known structure depending on how the Query is composed. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a> shows the Query structure. The presented experiences in this paper use the structure <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 18.982em; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">{\hbox{1000}}\cdot {\hbox{1}}\cdot {\hbox{01}}\cdot {\hbox{1}}\cdot {\hbox{00}}\cdot {\hbox{00}}\cdot {\hbox{0}}\cdot {\hbox{0000}}\cdot {\hbox{01101}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The process to configure favorable values of BLF, the data encoding, and the preamble is detailed below.</p><p>The first four bits 1000 allow identifying the command as the Query command and the last five bits 01101 corresponds to the cyclic redundancy check (CRC5) for error detecting; which depends of the information content. The information content is the sequence of bits between the Query command identifier and the CRC5. Inside the information sequence, there are three parameters for configuring a favorable tag response.</p><p>The bit in the fifth position, called the divide ratio (DR), determines where the BLF is defined. The value that the fifth bit can take “0” or “1” is traduced in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-56" role="math" style="width: 3.907em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.486em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.43em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-57"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-58" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">D</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-59" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-60" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-61" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">8</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">DR=8</script></tex-math></inline-formula> or <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-62" role="math" style="width: 5.529em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.988em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.93em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-63"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-64" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">D</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-65" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-66" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-67" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">64</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-68"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-69"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-70" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">/</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-71" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">3</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">DR=64/3</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively. In the analysis of the PSD, the BLF, which is the spectral distance between the CW component and the tag response, will be higher when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-72" role="math" style="width: 1.745em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.57em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-73"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-74" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">D</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-75" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">DR</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is higher. The calculation of the BLF is determined by the ratio <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-76" role="math" style="width: 6.249em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.589em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.59em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-77"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-78"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-79"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-80" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">D</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-81" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-82" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-83" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-84"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-85" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-86" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">T</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-87" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-88" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-89" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">l</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">{\rm DR}={\rm RTcal}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-90" role="math" style="width: 10.093em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 9.072em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1009.07em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-91"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-92"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-93"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-94" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-95" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">T</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-96" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-97" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-98" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">l</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-99" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-100" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">5</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-101" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">:</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-102" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">5</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-103" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-104" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-105"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-106" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">T</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-107" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-108" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-109" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">i</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-6">{\rm RTcal}=5:5\times {\rm Tari}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-110" role="math" style="width: 2.105em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.865em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.87em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-111"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-112"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-113"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-114" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">T</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-115" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-116" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-117" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">i</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-7">{\rm Tari}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the reference time interval for reader to tag signaling and is equal to the duration of data “0” <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_3b">[6]</a>. The couple of bits in sixth and seventh position is called <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-118" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.02em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-119"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-120"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-121"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-122" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">M<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-8">{M}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and sets the tag to reader data rate and encoding to which the tag responds. The couple of bits is set to “01,” which traduces into <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-9-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-123" role="math" style="width: 3.246em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.886em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.83em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-124"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-125"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-126"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-127" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">M<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-128" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-129" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-9">{M}=2</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and instructs the tag to respond using Miller coding with two cycles per bit, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>. Finally, the eighth bit position called <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-10-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-130" role="math" style="width: 3.126em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.826em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.77em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-131"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-132"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-133"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-134" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">T</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-135" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-136" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">e</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-137" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">x</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-138" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-10">{\rm TRext}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> achieves the periodic sequence of bits on the tag response. When <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-139" role="math" style="width: 3.246em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.886em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.83em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-140"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-141" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">M<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-142" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-143" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-11">M=2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-12-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-144" role="math" style="width: 6.369em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.709em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.59em 2.405em -999.997em); padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-154" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-155"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-156" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">"</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-157" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-158"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-159"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-160" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">"</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-162"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-163" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">M<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-164" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-165" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-13">M=2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-14-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-166" role="math" style="width: 6.369em; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-14">{\rm TRext}=\hbox{"}1\hbox{"}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the RN16 response prefixes an extended preamble of 16 bits of data “0” with two cycles per bit defined by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-15-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-183" role="math" style="width: 3.246em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.886em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1002.83em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-184"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-185" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">M<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-186" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-187" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-15">M=2</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a> shows the extended preamble scheme. The periodic sequence has approximately 65-<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-16-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-188" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.625em 1000.96em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-189"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-190" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">μ</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-191"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-192"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-193"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-194"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-195" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-16">\mu{\hbox {s}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> duration (depending on <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-17-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-196" role="math" style="width: 2.105em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.865em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1001.87em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-197"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-198"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-199"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-200" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">T</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-201" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-202" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-203" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">i</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-17">{\rm Tari}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>), which is enough to make the PSD calculation. Other parameters on the Query command were not configured since these are used for inventory purposes when the Select command is previously sent, which is not the case. Anyway, the values of these remaining parameters do not alter the results.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4 </b><fig><p>Query command structure <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_3b">[6]</a>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5 </b><fig><p>Miller sequence for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-18-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-204" role="math" style="width: 3.376em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.649em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.392em 1002.58em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-205"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-206"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-207"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-208" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">M<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.069em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-209" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-210" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.004em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-18">{M}=2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_3b">[6]</a>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6 </b><fig><p>Tag <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-19-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-211" role="math" style="width: 1.26em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.995em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.524em 1000.93em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-212"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-213" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">→</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.838em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-19">\rightarrow</script></tex-math></inline-formula> Reader preamble with Miller <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-214" role="math" style="width: 3.376em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.649em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.392em 1002.58em 2.45em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-215"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-216"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-217"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-218" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">M<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.069em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-219" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-220" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.079em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.004em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-20">{M}=2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_3b">[6]</a>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3c"><h3>C. Measurement System</h3><p>The measurement system includes a signal generator Agilent N5182A for synthesized RFID signal or an Alien Reader ALR-9780 <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref17" id="context_ref_17_3c">[17]</a> for real RFID signals, an RF amplifier Empower BBS314AAj with 41-dB gain, a 12-GHz digital storage oscilloscope (DSO) Agilent 91204A (40 Gsamples/s), and a PC for control and data processing. The set of signal generator and PC is called the RFID tester; this configuration allows handling of the Query command. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a> shows the measurement setup in the anechoic chamber with a partition wall that offers 48-dB isolation between horn antennas to minimize the mutual coupling.
</p><ul style="list-style-type:disc"><li><p>The element-under-test (EUT) tag is located at a distance of 1 m from each horn antenna and oriented for maximum reception and reradiation.</p></li><li><p>The forward link signal is generated by only one of two ways: in synthesized signals, the baseband command generated by Matlab is transferred to the signal generator where it is modulated, amplified, and sent to the tag via the transmitting antenna; in signals coming from an RFID reader, an ALR-9780 reader is set to replace the signal generator.</p></li><li><p>The return link signal is always collected by the receiving antenna, observed and analyzed in the RF band on the DSO. In compliance with the EPC Class1 Gen2 standard, the synthesized signal carries the Query command. In the case of signals coming from an RFID reader, the RFID air interface cannot be parameterized and a standard handshake is made between the reader and tag <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_3c">[6]</a>.</p></li></ul>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7 </b><fig><p>(a) Measurement setup in bistatic configuration. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-21-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-221" role="math" style="width: 1.789em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.392em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.26em 1001.39em 2.583em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-222"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-223"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.392em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.046em 1000.73em 4.17em -999.997em); top: -3.965em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-224" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">A</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.833em; left: 0.731em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-225"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-226"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-227" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">G</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.329em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.254em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-21">A_{G}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the horn antenna gain. (b) Setup distribution on the anechoic chamber.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The amplifier was used only in power dependency tests, presented in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec6c" class="fulltext-link">Section VI-C</a>.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3d"><h3>D. Considered Tags</h3><p>In order to validate the measurement procedure, nine different commercially tags (inlays) were chosen. Tags are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a> and details are listed on <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8 </b><fig><p>Time-domain response from nine UHF RFID tags.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>From the two possible options shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>, in case of absence of the tag only the carrier component is expected on the PSD analysis. Contrary, when there is an activated tag, the power of the first sidelobe around the CW in the PSD analysis is considered as the power of the modulated tag response. The calculation of the PSD is repeated over the harmonics of the CW until the fifth harmonic order on each tag. The implemented modulation for all the studied tags is the amplitude shift keying (ASK) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_3d">[6]</a>.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3e"><h3>E. Power Budget</h3><p>The power budget in the band of 868–922 MHz considering the measurement setup of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a> is described below. Antennas gain <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-228" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.38em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-229"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-230"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.72em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-231" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">A</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-232"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-233"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-234" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">G</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-22">A_{G}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> varies increasingly between 5.69–6.69 dBi on 868–922 MHz, respectively.
</p><ul style="list-style-type:disc"><li><p>In transmission: losses in cables 1–3 including connectors are 0.73, 0.73, and 1.45 dB, respectively; The amplifier when used, inserts a gain of 41 dB.</p></li><li><p>In reception: losses in cables 4 and 5 are 0.73 and 1.46 dB, respectively.</p></li><li><p>The noise level inside the anechoic chamber is around −110 dBm.</p></li></ul><p></p><p>The power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-235" role="math" style="width: 1.925em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.745em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.75em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-236"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-237"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.745em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-238" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-239"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-240"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-241" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-242" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-243" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-23">P_{\rm out}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> delivered by the RFID tester or the reader is varied according to each tag activation needs. Considering the power budget in transmission and reception and the free-space path loss <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1" href="#deqn1" class="fulltext-link">(1)</a> at distance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-244" role="math" style="width: 0.904em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.784em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1000.78em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-245"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-246" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">R</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-24">R</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of 1 m and the wavelength <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-247" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1000.6em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-248"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-249" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">λ</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-25">\lambda</script></tex-math></inline-formula> at each frequency in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">Table II</a>, then it is possible to calculate each tag sensitivity <disp-formula id="deqn1" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-250" role="math" style="width: 100%; display: inline-block; min-width: 13.396em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 100%; height: 0px; font-size: 111%; min-width: 13.396em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(2.405em 1009.19em 5.168em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em; width: 100%;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-251"><span class="mtable" id="MathJax-Span-252" style="min-width: 13.396em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 100%; height: 0px; min-width: 13.396em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 9.252em; height: 0px; clip: rect(-1.619em 1009.19em 1.144em -999.997em); top: 0.003em; left: 50%; margin-left: -4.622em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(2.405em 1009.19em 5.168em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 9.252em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(2.405em 1009.19em 5.168em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 50%; margin-left: -4.622em;"><span class="mtd" id="MathJax-Span-262"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-263"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-264" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-265" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-266" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">20</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-267" style="padding-left: 0.183em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.045em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1001.26em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-268" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">log</span><span style="display: inline-block; <div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Radar Cross Section (RCS) and Physical Area of an RFID Tag</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4a"><h3>A. RCS and Tag Dimensions</h3><p>The RCS of the tag or echo area is defined as the area intercepting that amount of power, which, when scattered isotropically, produces at the receiver a density that is equal to that scattered by the actual object. The RCS <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-29-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-303" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; position: relative; width: 4.267em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.9em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-688" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">K<span style="display: inline-block; The <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta {\rm RCS}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-717" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-718"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-719" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-720"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-721"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-722" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-723" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-724" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">S</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">\Delta {\rm RCS}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> evaluates the functional characteristics of the tag as read range or sensitivity because it is related to the efficiency of the backscattering modulation technique <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_4a">[2]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_4a">[4]</a>. Finally, the physical area <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">A_{p}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-52-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-725" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-53">\varepsilon_{ap}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> shown in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn8" href="#deqn8" class="fulltext-link">(8)</a> as follows: <disp-formula id="deqn8" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\varepsilon_{ap}={A_{e}\over A_{p}}.\eqno{\hbox{(8)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processed"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-740" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; right: 0.003em;"><span class="mtd" id="mjx-eqn-${\hbox{(8)}}$"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-744"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-745"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-746"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-747"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-748"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-749"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-750"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-751" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(8)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; Experimental Validation</h3><p>From <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn6" href="#deqn6" class="fulltext-link">(6)</a> and <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn8" href="#deqn8" class="fulltext-link">(8)</a>, by considering the physical area of the tag antenna for a given tag, greater resonance surface means greater effective area then higher RCS. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a> shows 20 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu{\hbox {s}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-775" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-776"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-777" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">μ</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-778"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-779"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-780"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-781"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-782" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">s</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-55">\mu{\hbox {s}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of tag response for the nine tags where the modulated backscatter is clearly distinguishable. Tag T1, which exhibits greater resonance surface, has a great scatter capability, and a higher RCS. In an ideal condition, when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">K=1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-783" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-784"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-785" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">K<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-786" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-787" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-56">K=1</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in the scavenging state, an antenna loaded with a complex-conjugate impedance load scatters the same amount of power as the load absorbs, thus causing a maximum <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta {\rm RCS}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-788" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-789"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-790" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-791"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-792"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-793" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-794" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-795" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">S</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-57">\Delta {\rm RCS}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Although all tags are illuminated with the same power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm out}=16.75\ {\hbox{dBm}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-58-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-796" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-797"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-798"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.745em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-799" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-800"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-801"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-802" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-803" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-804" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-805" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-806" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">16.75</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-807" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-808"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-809"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-810"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-811"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-812" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-58">P_{\rm out}=16.75\ {\hbox{dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, it is highlighted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a> that the amplitudes, directly related with the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta {\rm RCS}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-59-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-813" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-814"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-815" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-816"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-817"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-818" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-819" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-820" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">S</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-59">\Delta {\rm RCS}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, vary up to 42%. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm out}=16.75\ {\hbox{dBm}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-60-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-821" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-822"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-823"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.745em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-824" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-825"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-826"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-827" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-828" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-829" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-830" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-831" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">16.75</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-832" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-833"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-834"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-835"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-836"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-837" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">P_{\rm out}=16.75\ {\hbox{dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> represents the power to activate the tag with less sensitivity, T4.</p><p>Consequently there are two factors involved on the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert\Delta {\rm RCS}\vert</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-838" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-839"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-840" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-841" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-842"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-843"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-844" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-845" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">C</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-846" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">S</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-847" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-61">\vert\Delta {\rm RCS}\vert</script></tex-math></inline-formula> variations <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn7" href="#deqn7" class="fulltext-link">(7)</a>:
</p><ul style="list-style-type:disc"><li><p>the matching degree between the antenna and IC load in the scavenging state;</p></li><li><p>the physical area of the antenna.</p></li></ul><p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>PSD Analysis in the RFID System</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec5a"><h3>A. PSD Properties</h3><p>The interpretation of the PSD is enhanced due to the contribution of the RFID physical layer setting achieving a periodic sequence of bits on the tag response. This implies that the characteristics of the modulated signal coming from the tag are enhanced on the observed window. In effect, in this case the amplitudes of the spectrum are maximal and the BLF is distinguishably positioned at 230 kHz from the CW. It should be noted that, for the following analysis, the power of the tag response will be quantified as the amplitude of first sidelobe. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 9</a>–<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link"></a><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">11</a> show examples of the PSD calculation while the communication reader-tag is established. The PSD at CW fundamental and its harmonic frequencies is compared with the PSD when no tag is present. In this last case, the observed CW is essentially due to the coupling between horns.</p><p>Two operational modes of the passive UHF RFID tag are defined in both states of modulation.
</p><ul style="list-style-type:disc"><li><p>The structural mode <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{S}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-62-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-848" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-849"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-850"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.02em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-851"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-852"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-853" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">M<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-854"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-855"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-856" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-62">{M}_{S}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> produced when the tag antenna is in matching condition. The scattered power contribution is always constant. In this mode, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">k=1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-63-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-857" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-858"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-859" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">k</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-860" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-861" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1</span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-63">k=1</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn2" href="#deqn2" class="fulltext-link">(2)</a></p></li><li><p>The antenna mode <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{A}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-64-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-862" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-863"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-864"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.02em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-865"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-866"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-867" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">M<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-868"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-869"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-870" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">A</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-64">{M}_{A}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is produced by the reradiated power reflected by the IC load into the tag antenna. The antenna mode depends upon the two values that the IC load impedance can take. In ideal matching conditions on the scavenging state, the structural mode is equal to the antenna mode.</p></li></ul><p></p><p>The scavenging state can be quantified in the PSD level at CW frequency. In the reflecting state only, the antenna mode changes. The PSD level of tag response in the reflecting state is observed at the BLF. On the harmonic analysis, these PSD properties are also valid to analyze the scavenging and reflecting states.</p><p>
