<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a> shows the PSD at 915 MHz. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 10</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">11</a> show the PSD at second harmonic of 1830 MHz and third harmonic of 2745 MHz for tag T5. The tag T5 was chosen because it has the higher PSD level at the third backscattered harmonic. In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 9</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">11</a>, the tag response with modulated information on the sidelobes like a typical spectrum of the square waves is clearly seen. In the case of the second harmonic in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a>, no response was noted at the activation power.<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec5b"><h3>B. Matching in Scavenging State</h3><p>In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a>, when there is a tag, the PSD level of CW at the fundamental frequency in the presence of a tag is 6.9 dB higher compared when there is no tag. The 6.9 dB are taken as the total contribution of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{M}_{S}+{M}_{A}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-68-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-922" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-923"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-924"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.505em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.02em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-925"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-926"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-927" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">M<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-928"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-929"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-930" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-931" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">+</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-932" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.565em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.02em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-933"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-934"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-935" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">M<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-936"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-937"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-938" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">A</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-68">{M}_{S}+{M}_{A}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The difference at the third harmonic is 3.27 dB in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 11</a>. On the PSD analysis, the matching in scavenging state can be quantified by the difference of levels at the CW frequency when there is a tag and when there is no tag. The difference has to be minimal representing only the RCS in the structural mode. Large differences indicate mismatching reflections. The difference assesses indirectly the RCS characteristics from each tag at fundamental and harmonic frequencies.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12</a> shows the PSD value on the CW fundamental frequency and CW harmonics for five representative tags until the fifth harmonic considering each tag sensibility. The mesh represents the measured CW power when no tag is present also until the fifth harmonic. A decreasing behavior is observed while the harmonic order increases. Only tag T1 is the exception, having a second backscattered harmonic weaker than the third, which reveals scavenging properties at the third harmonic. Tag T5 has the best scavenging performance, i.e., the better matching at the third harmonic according to the criterion of minimal difference of PSD levels at the CW frequency.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig12"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-12-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-12-small.gif" alt="Figure 12" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 12 </b><fig><p>Measured PSD at CW harmonic frequencies with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm out}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-69-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-939" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-940"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-941"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.723em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.112em 1000.73em 4.17em -999.997em); top: -3.965em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-942" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.136em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.833em; left: 0.665em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-943"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-944"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-945" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-946" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-947" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-69">P_{\rm out}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> considering each tag sensibility.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>In the performed setup, the PSD calculation at the CW frequency represents the coupling between the horn antennas, which reveals CW harmonics coming from the RFID tester. Scatter capabilities of each tag varies the level of the observed CW that depends on each tag RCS.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec5c"><h3>C. Backscattered Harmonics</h3><p>The level at the BLF in the PSD analysis at each CW harmonic represents the backscattered harmonics in the reflecting state. It is important to explain the basis of harmonic radiation of the tag antenna usually designed as an optimization process of a half-wave dipole at fundamental frequency. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 13</a> shows the harmonic current distributions on a half-wave dipole working at fundamental frequency, which shows that, for even harmonics, the current at the antenna input is zero. Although if even harmonics were present from the IC, they would not be efficiently reradiated since the half-wave dipole would require zero admitance at even harmonics, in fact, practically impossible <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref27" id="context_ref_27_5c">[27]</a>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig14" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 14</a> shows the level contributed by five representative tags on its modulated response at each harmonic frequency. In all cases, the fundamental and third harmonic response are predominant. Even though fifth is an odd harmonic, it has a hardly distinguishable level. The affirmation of a perceptible third harmonic backscattered carrying information is then valid. The higher power of the first sidelobe on third backscattered harmonic is for tag T5 with −86.03 dBm. Considering this value, there were not significant second harmonics. <a ref-type="table" anchor="table3" class="fulltext-link">Table III</a> summarizes the results for the second and third harmonics for all tags regarding each tag sensitivity.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig13"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-13-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-13-small.gif" alt="Figure 13" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 13 </b><fig><p>Current distribution until fifth harmonic along the length of a half-wave dipole designed for fundamental frequency. The half-wave dipole requires zero admitance at even harmonics to be able to radiate.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig14"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-14-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-14-small.gif" alt="Figure 14" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 14 </b><fig><p>PSD of the tag response at the BLF. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm out}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-70-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-948" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-949"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-950"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.723em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.112em 1000.73em 4.17em -999.997em); top: -3.965em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-951" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.136em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.833em; left: 0.665em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-952"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-953"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-954" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-955" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-956" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-70">P_{\rm out}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> considers each tag sensibility.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full table" id="table3"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table III </b>Backscattered Harmonics from Tag Response<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-table-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-table-3-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div><p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec6"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VI.</div><h2>Dependency Analysis of Harmonic Scattering</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec6a"><h3>A. Dependency on Operation at the Fundamental Frequency</h3><p>Analyzing the harmonic performance respect to the results at the fundamental frequency, <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a> presents tag T1 with the best performance at fundamental frequency. However, the analysis, made in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5c" class="fulltext-link">Section V-C</a>, presents tag T5 with the higher third backscattered harmonic. The performance of the tag depends basically on the antenna-IC load matching and its physical characteristics <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn7" href="#deqn7" class="fulltext-link">(7)</a> at the frequency of interest. Since the tag antenna has different designs, some of them can be close to a matching situation on some odd harmonics profiting the current distribution over the dipole shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 13</a>, especially the third one due its level. A certain degree of matching at the harmonic frequency may cause the antenna to reradiate the harmonics produced by the IC, but there is not direct dependency between the performance at fundamental and backscattered harmonics.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec6b"><h3>B. Bits Sequence Dependency</h3><p>Achieving the manipulation of the RFID air interface to reproduce tag responses with different bit structures enables the development of a bit sequence dependency analysis. The dependency on the sequence of bits on the harmonic backscattered is studied by calculating the PSD over a random bits sequence, by randomly choosing a portion of the RN16 response instead of the preamble. Therefore, the comparison of PSD was made on two different sequences when <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm out}=16.75\ {\hbox{dBm}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-71-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-957" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-958"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-959"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.745em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-960" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-961"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-962"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-963" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-964" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-965" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-966" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-967" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">16.75</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-968" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-969"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-970"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-971"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-972"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-973" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-71">P_{\rm out}=16.75\ {\hbox{dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig15" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 15</a> shows the PSD comparison at fundamental frequency for tag T5. As expected, the sidelobes in the periodic sequences are thin and powerful compared to those in the random sequences. The same behavior is observed for the third harmonic in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig16" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 16</a>. In order to compare the power levels of the modulated tag response until fifth harmonic from periodic and random sequences, <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig17" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 17</a> shows the data for tag T5. The PSD level of periodic signals is higher until fourth harmonic. In the fifth harmonic, the relation is inverse, but close to the noise level. The sequence of bits transmitted by the tag then influences directly on the backscattered harmonics. The merit of the air interface configuration is that it can reproduce a tag response carrying a periodic sequence of bits over all EPC Class 1 Gen2 tags facilitating the PSD analysis. Looking into applications, the use of periodic sequences can be an advantage to achieve a distinguishable power to distinguish signals from different sources or positions.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec6c"><h3>C. Reader Power Dependency</h3><p>
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig15"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-15-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-15-small.gif" alt="Figure 15" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 15 </b><fig><p>PSD of periodic and random sequence response for tag T5 at fundamental frequency.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig16"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-16-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-16-small.gif" alt="Figure 16" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 16 </b><fig><p>PSD of periodic and random sequence response for tag T5 at third harmonic.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig17"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-17-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-17-small.gif" alt="Figure 17" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 17 </b><fig><p>Comparison of PSD level from periodic and random sequence response for tag T5.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
The reader power dependency is studied by varying <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm out}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-72-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-974" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-975"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-976"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.745em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-977" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-978"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-979"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-980" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-981" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-982" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-72">P_{\rm out}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from the minimum level to activate the tag with less sensibility until a maximum value to reach the equipment limit or saturate the tag. No low-pass filter was used at the reader output in order to reproduce a normal scenery in compliance of the EPC Class 1 Gen2 standard regarding the transmitted power level at fundamental and spurious bands. For this experience, two sources were considered: (1) RFID tester and (2) ALR-9780 reader. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig18" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 18</a> shows the comparison of both sources. The second CW harmonic and third CW harmonic from the reader are even 14 and 2 dB greater than the RFID tester, respectively, for fourth and fifth, the reader gives around 8-dB greater power. A second set of tests was performed, this time introducing the amplifier after the signal generator, which allows evaluations on wide ranges of power. The amplifier introduces 41 dB of gain. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm out}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-73-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-983" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-984"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-985"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.745em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-986" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-987"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-988"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-989" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-990" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-991" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-73">P_{\rm out}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is first set to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm out}=-24.2\ {\hbox{dBm}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-74-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-992" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-993"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-994"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.745em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-995" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-996"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-997"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-998" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-999" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1000" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1001" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1002" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">−</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1003" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">24.2</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1004" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1005"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1006"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1007"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1008"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1009" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-74">P_{\rm out}=-24.2\ {\hbox{dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which represents an average power of operation high enough to work with all available tags. An increment of 19.2 dB, which means <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{\rm out}=-5\ {\hbox{dBm}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-75-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1010" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1011"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1012"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.745em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1013" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1014"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1015"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1016" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1017" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">u</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1018" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1019" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1020" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">−</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1021" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">5</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1022" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;"> </span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1023"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1024"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1025"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1026"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1027" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-75">P_{\rm out}=-5\ {\hbox{dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, does not affect the strength of the tag response at the fundamental frequency, as can be seen in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig19" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 19</a>, but only affects the level at CW frequency. constructively for the second and third harmonic of the tag response. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig20" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 20</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig21" class="fulltext-link">21</a> contrarily show that this effect clearly. The backscattered harmonics then depends directly on the power level that the reader transmits. Two reasons can explain this effect both based on the increment of harmonic level from the reader.
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig18"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-18-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-18-small.gif" alt="Figure 18" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 18 </b><fig><p>Comparison of harmonic levels generated from the RFID tester and one commercial reader.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig19"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-19-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-19-small.gif" alt="Figure 19" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 19 </b><fig><p>Effect of the transmitted power on the backscattered response at fundamental frequency.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<ul style="list-style-type:disc"><li><p>By increasing the reader power, the input impedance of the IC load changes because of its nonlinear behavior, and this changes the matching with the antenna. Depending on this, the shunt transistor, which regulates the internal supply voltage of the logic part, receives power to activate it and works increasing until its upper power limit <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref28" id="context_ref_28_6c">[28]</a>.</p></li><li><p>The tag could respond at the harmonic Query. The effect in which the tag responds at various frequencies is called the frequency diverse backscatter property and is explained in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref29" id="context_ref_29_6c">[29]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref30" id="context_ref_30_6c">[30]</a>.</p></li></ul>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig20"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-20-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-20-small.gif" alt="Figure 20" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 20 </b><fig><p>Effect of the transmitted power on the second backscattered harmonic.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig21"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-21-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-21-small.gif" alt="Figure 21" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 21 </b><fig><p>Effect of the transmitted power on the third backscattered harmonic.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec6d"><h3>D. Frequency-Hopping Dependency</h3><p>The frequency-hopping spread-spectrum (FHSS) technique is based on the automatic hopping of the CW frequency at brief time intervals. The frequency is chosen in a pseudorandom way from a set of frequencies covering much wider band than the bandwidth required to transmit the signal containing the useful data. In the U.S., according to the current Federal Communications Commission (FCC) regulation, the FHSS can be used to sweep the frequency band from 902 to 928 MHz with 500-kHz width per channel <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref22" id="context_ref_22_6d">[22]</a>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig22" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 22</a> shows the PSD level at fundamental CW frequencies over the entire U.S. band for tags T1, T4, and T5. The top curves represent the PSD at the CW frequency and the bottom curves represent the PSD level at the BLF. The CW level varies 3 dB over the entire band. The bottom curves, however, are almost constant. As was described before, the impedance of the IC load varies according to the received power. This variation is capable of helping or hurting the IC performance at fundamental harmonic depending on the tag antenna impedance bandwidth. In this case, the 3-dB variations on the CW level are not affecting the tag response on the U.S. band. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig23" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 23</a> shows the PSD level at third CW harmonics for the same tags T1, T4, and T5. The PSD level at BLF on the third harmonic varies until 10 dB while the PSD level at the BLF varies 5 dB. The nonconstant level of the tag response at the third harmonic is consistent since the tag impedance bandwidth is not tuned over this band.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig22"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-22-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-22-small.gif" alt="Figure 22" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 22 </b><fig><p>Power on frequency-hopping channels.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig23"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-23-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/6522526/6512619/6512619-fig-23-small.gif" alt="Figure 23" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 23 </b><fig><p>Power at the harmonics of the frequency-hopping channels.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6512619/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The variations of PSD level at BLF on the third harmonic band shows an indirect relation with the FHSS channel. The indirect relation states that there is a major cause: it is in fact the matching degree at the third harmonic. The PSD level at the BLF also depends on the channel conditions, which are different in each band due to fading phenomenon <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref31" id="context_ref_31_6d">[31]</a>. There is then not direct dependency on the FHSS technique.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec7"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VII.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>A practical experimentation of the nonlinearities in the RFID UHF system was performed. The measurement procedure is based on the PSD analysis performing a temporal acquisition directly in the RF band while the communication tag to reader is fully established. By setting the Query parameters, it is possible to manipulate the RFID physical layer in order to facilitate the PSD interpretation. The PSD calculation reveals harmonics on the return signal consequence of the not treated nonlinearity effects of the IC. It was also noted harmonics generated by the reader in the forward signal. The uncontrolled nonlinearity in the current UHF RFID technology allows the tag to generate harmonics signals carrying information without constraints to the EPC Global Class 1 Gen 2 standard. The backscattered harmonics are independent of the performance at the fundamental harmonic and of the FHSS transmission technique, but depend on the power sent by the reader and the sequence of bits that the tag transmits.</p><p>The analysis made on this paper considers the entire tag (antenna and IC) as the EUT. The analysis evaluates the nonlinearity characteristic of a generic UHF RFID EPC Class1 Gen2 IC without constraints for one specific kind of IC. The characterization of the IC alone may become the topic of future work in order to assess harmonic generation depending on the kind of IC. With the presence of harmonics carrying information, a redundant passive RFID system could be declared, where the characteristics of the signal through a new propagation channel introduces more information, e.g., in security, sensoring, or localization applications.</p></div>
</div></div>

					<!-- ngRepeat: biop in ::item.bio.p --><div class="pure-u-24-24 u-mt-1 ng-binding ng-scope" ng-repeat="biop in ::item.bio.p">Smail Tedjini (SM'92) received the Doctor in Physics degree from the Grenoble Institute of Technology (Grenoble INP), Grenoble, France, in 1985.</div><!-- end ngRepeat: biop in ::item.bio.p --><div class="pure-u-24-24 u-mt-1 ng-binding ng-scope" ng-repeat="biop in ::item.bio.p">From 1982 to 1986, he was an Assistant Professor with Grenoble INP. From 1986 to 1993, he was Senior Researcher with the CNRS-IMEP Laboratory. From 1993 to 1996, he was a Professor with the University Joseph Fourier of Grenoble. Since 1996, he has been a Professor with the Engineering School ESISAR (a part of Grenoble INP). His teaching topics concern applied electromagnetism, and circuits and systems for RF, wireless, and opto-electronics. He has authored or coauthored over 250 publications, among them more than 150 international papers and communications. His past research activities have concerned the modeling of devices and circuits at both RF and opto-electronic domains. His current research interests is a Laboratoire de Conception et d’Intégration des Systèmes (LCIS) focus on wireless systems with specific attention to RFID technologies and applications. He was at the origin of several research activities and groups with Grenoble INP (IMEP Laboratory and LCIS Laboratory). In 1996, he founded the LCIS Laboratory, where he was the Director from 1996 to 2000 and Director of ESISAR from 2006 to 2007. He conducted several research contracts with industry and public administrations. He has supervised over 30 Ph.D. theses and served as an examiner/reviewer for numerous Ph.D. theses in many countries.</div><!-- end ngRepeat: biop in ::item.bio.p --><div class="pure-u-24-24 u-mt-1 ng-binding ng-scope" ng-repeat="biop in ::item.bio.p">Prof. Tedjini is a member of several Technical Program Committees (TPCs) and serves as an expert/reviewer for national and international scientific committees and conferences including ISO, Piers, IEEE, URSI, ISO, EuCap, ANR, OSEO, FNQRT, etc. He has organized several conferences/workshops. He is past president and founder of the IEEE-CPMT French Chapter and vice president of the IEEE Section France. In 2008, he was vice chair of URSI Commission D, Electronics and Photonics. From 2011 to 2014, he will be serving as vice chair of the IEEE France Section and chair of URSI Commission D for the triennium.</div><!-- end ngRepeat: biop in ::item.bio.p -->

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

		}
	}
});

The main objective is to analyze the harmonics produced by the chip and radiated by the tag antenna. From experimentation, the characteristics of the nonlinearities contained in the signals are highlighted and linked to the theory of the backscattering in the RFID context. Several experiences taking into account the standards are proposed. Moreover, several commercial tags are considered in order to compare the observations. The used configuration, the experimental setup, and the protocols are described in detail. In particular, the generation of periodic and reproducible sequences of bits is introduced and its advantages are emphasized. Finally, contrarily to the classic approaches that tend to eliminate the harmonics generated by the rectifiers of tags, the great interest of the possible exploitation of backscattered harmonics is
